Found this song from the comments on a Rev Says Desu video, and honestly, this just adds to the pile of motivation to create my Worlds, and share them for everyone to see. Now it brings up the question; just how much motivation do I need in order to get me to actually share it? I've got these whole worlds, fitting every description I hear from people for what they enjoy seeing in content, and even filling spots that I feel would completely change the market, but I just can't get myself to actually turn these worlds into a tangible experience for others to enjoy. I've got all the characters, all the plans, all the skills, all the resources, and all the motivation, as well as constantly getting the urge to do it, but I just. . . Can't do it. What am I missing? Support? I would say what I need is an audience to tell me to do it, and support from that audience, but I know that that only comes from work. Hard work, the very work that I need that support for. Maybe it's my refusal to cheat or self-promote. I have something driving me to do it, but it just isnt working. I have all the motivation in the world, hundreds and thousands of voices telling me indirectly that I have what they are searching for, but I just can't bring it into their reach. I feel like this might be going on for too long, but I felt the need to express this somewhere, and just get it off my chest. Hey, maybe sharing this will finally fulfill whatever I need to get the work done. But before I close off this comment, I would like to add; this is not me asking for an audience. This is not me asking you to support me. I want to earn it myself. But I just needed to get this out there, and maybe finally saying this will open the floodgates and allow me to bring my own worlds to life. If you are interested, then cool. If you _choose_ to go out of your way to go to my channel, cool. But I'd rather you just wait until I show up on your reccomended, where I can earn the audience legit. I'd rather you just, take this as motivation, I guess. Know that all it takes is to finally open the gates, and chances are, there will be an audience, and rather than spambotting youtube links, or trying to get clicks from Shock value(I swear if one of those spambots ends up on this comment, it's getting *all* the pure and utter loathsome hatred that I've been keeping inside), I intend to _earn_ that audience.  Here's a little _truly_ motivational quote for you;  You may not be able to succeed, you might never be discovered. But if you don't at least try, you make that might, go to nothing. Everything you can create has an audience out there. You just gotta find it. And if you don't create, you won't ever reach them. If you think you aren't creative; you're wrong. _everybody_ can create. We live in the world of innovation, and as long as you have a functioning brain, you can learn to create. Can't code? No problem, just follow a course or guide online. Can't draw? Well right there, you are just lying to yourself. Just *_try_* and if you aren't happy with that drawing, then fix what was wrong with it. If the drawing is fundamentally flawed at its core, then you didn't try. And no, simple stick-figures are not trying But if you can draw stick figures in different poses, that right there is enough, as then all you need is a story. Then you can share that story with the world through animation. Can't animate? Bullsh*t, you can move, and if you're reading this, you probably have a way to record yourself. Even if you have only one limb, you can still do it, it just takes more time. You csn Motion Capture yourself, and apply those animations to 3D models. And if you only have one limb, then you _definitely_ have a story to tell. If you had a rough life, you can take inspiration from that. If you're a stuck-up spoiled snob that's full of themself, all it would take is to get off your high horse and you can take an idea and run with it, 'cause that lifestyle means you've got money to spare, so you can do _anything_ with ease. But even if you're poor, you have _some_ kind of technology, for you to be reading this, and that is all you need. Computer? Get OBS and some free game off the internet and do let's plays, earn a living, and from there,  you can upgrade. And if you've already got worlds waiting to be released, all you need is to share those worlds, and chances are, you will succeed. Be better than me, and get out there, _share_ what you create.

Calliope isn't saying you should give up because you'll never make it she's saying you need to bring some of your passion to the table as well as put in the hard work. Its a very competitive field to be making content in so you need to be willing to stick it through and work hard.

Ğ—Ğ°ĞµĞ±Ğ¸ÑÑŒ, Ñ‡Ñ‘Ñ‚ĞºĞ¾!
You don't even remember exactly why you were climbing this mountain anymore.  All that you do know now is the burning ache that permeates every nerve in your legs, as they buckle beneath you, forcing you onto your knees. the frigid air around you nearly freezing your own sweat to your body, sending wave after wave of chills up your spine. As you wrap your arms around yourself, the old, rusted katana you've been carrying clatters to the ground next to you. That's what it was. You were climbing this mountain, because you heard tales of a legendary dojo at the summit, that could turn the lowliest armature into a skilled master in a matter of months.  You had searched before for a great sensei, yet none seemed to live up to your expectations. They all went much too slow for your tastes. You wanted the best of the best. Not only that, but the legend states that you need not pay for this training, should you make it to the dojo in the first place. And with how poor your family is, and your picky attitude, this seems the only viable option.   You look back behind you as the cold continues to drive daggers through your body. Perhaps you should've settled? Taken the first sensei you could find? It certainly would've saved you all the suffering you're feeling now.  No. You erase the very thoughts from your brain. You've come too far. There is no way you're giving up now. As you shakily put your feet under yourself once more, using your family's only, heirloom sword as a crutch, every fiber of your being screams once more for you to turn back. Your feet have never hurt this much in your life. However, as you continue walking for what seems like an eternity, you spot it. A small building, built onto the side of the mountain. Through the driving snow you can see the lights, flickering from inside. You made it. It's right in front of you!  With eyes on the prize, the exhaustion evaporates, and you break into a full sprint towards the dojo, getting closer and closer, until you eventually sink to your knees once again in front of the door. Panting, you slide it out of the way, to see a warmly lit interior that, despite the mountain climate, is strangely comfortable inside. As if it were spring back on ground. Looking around you see naught but tatami mats covering the floor, as well as a singular wall over on the right, covered from top to bottom in various weapons and armor. The most displayed however, is an elegantly crafted scythe, hung front and center on the wall, adorned with designs of rose petals and sakura flowers.   It is only then that you notice on the left a stout woman wearing a starkly colored kimono, with staggeringly pink hair. She is sitting at the table under a kotatsu, sipping freshly brewed tea. As she lowers the cup, her gaze meets yours, and she stands, and walks over to you. Could this be the master of the legend?  Before you can stand to bow to her, she is already towering over you, leering down at you face.   "Another student, hmm?" She purrs, her face showing a slight grin. "You wish to learn from me?"  "Yes sensei!" You shout as you prostrate yourself before her. "I've heard from many a legend that you can turn even the weakest amature into the greatest master. Your strength is uncanny."  Without a word she walks over to the display wall, and causally removes the scythe from it, holding it in her fairly petite hands. "And what makes you think you are worthy to learn from me?"  "Well, I climbed the mountain! Isn't that proof of my dedication? Now you know how much I wish to learn!"  Within a flash, the woman is right in front of you. "And how do you think *I* got up here?"   With not another word she swings the blunt side of her scythe into your chest, knocking you out the door and back into the snow.  "Go back home." she says, "You're not worthy."  After she slams the door in your face, you begin your decent down the mountain. It's much easier than going up.   As you make your way back to your house, night has fallen over the village. Walking into you family's home, you head directly to your room, and as you fall asleep, you contemplate once again giving up. However, catching a last glimpse of your family sword before you drift off, your resolve strengthens once more.  The next day you climb the mountain again, and eventually arrive again at the dojo. You ask the woman a second time to teach you, and she once more declines. However, before she can hit you with her scythe, you use the katana in your hand to block the strike. However, it is not enough, and she knocks you out the door once again.  You continue this routine, day after day, week after week. Each day you arrive, climbing the mountain becomes easier and easier, leaving you more energetic for the fight ahead of you. Each week, you manage to block more and more strikes, until eventually you are able to strike back. After a few months of this routine, asking each day to be taught, you eventually manage to knock the woman to the ground during your daily fight.  Holding the rusted, chipped point of your sword to the woman's chest, you say, "Will you teach me now, sensei."  "I should be calling you that." She chuckles. "Don't you see? You no longer need my teaching. You've finished, and you've passed."  And then it hits you. Each day from the first, your resolve grew stronger and stronger. Each climb and each fight gave you greater and greater skill. You look down at your body, and you see the great amount of muscle you've put on, as well as the great amount of scars. You've never been this fit in your life.  You look down once again at the woman, and hold out your hand to help her up. As you help her to her feet, she bows to you, taking you by complete shock.   "This place is yours now. You are now the Master of the Mountain. I shall take my scythe, and take my leave. This dojo has all the accommodations you will need to stay here as you may."   As you look down at your sword, you see that inexplicably, it has been polished to a sheen, and sharpened to the point that you can hear it cutting the dust in the air. As the woman removes her scythe, the stand resizes itself, to a size that would fit your katana perfectly.  "You may have beaten me," she begins, "but don't relax yet. I will be back tomorrow."  Edit: Thanks Everyone for the support! I don't really write that much in my free time, but when something tickles my inspiration bone like this song, I can just let the words flow! I'll try writing more when I have the time!

I kinda wanted to post the same comment here. I don't think it really needs saying, but I will say it anyway; Calli deserves every bit of attention she has gotten, as do all of the other members of Hololive. The amount of time and effort these girls put into their streams, music, and art shouldn't discounted or ignored. We Deadbeats, KFP employees, Chumbuddies, Teamates, and Tentacultists are grateful for your girls' dedication as entertainers. cool cool  Pasted comment begins here:  "Her success isn't down to herself it's because of hololive." [this is an excerpt of a tweet highlighted in the video mentioned above]  I mean, to a certain extent, this is sort of true. Hololive gave her a huge amount of attention. But at the same time, she was already very skilled and pretty successful when it came to her music BEFORE she joined Hololive, which is why Hololive accepted her in the first place. Cover doesn't just hire randos off the street. She worked her ass off for years, and Hololive sort of gave her the big break she deserved.   This whole claim is similar to this little hypothetical example:  Mangaka makes very good manga. Manga gets adapted into an anime. The anime adaptation is successful and in return gives the manga and mangaka more attention. Critics claim the only reason the mangaka is successful is because his manga got an anime adaptation. Except the reason why his work got an anime in the first place was because it was already very good and successful enough to get notices and picked up.  Like yes, part of the reason why he is really successful now is directly because of the anime adaptation. But that animation adaptation would've never happened if he didn't already have the skill to make a good, successful manga.  The end.  song is a banger tho

So after hearing this song a few times, an inspiration hit me that I haven't seen anybody else comment on it, a little blurb in the lyrics that nobody else seems to have caught:  Later in the song, she goes "though this hell is ten times hotter than the start" .... this, to me, is saying that Calli's life is _even harder_ now that she is a part of Hololive and it's kind of like a lightbulb moment. The standards and demands placed on her now that she is employed by Hololive are higher than what they were when she was independent. She got hired by Hololive, yes, but she has to _maintain_ that. She can't just sit back and relax now that she's joined a company. She has to push herself to do better, to put out content worthy of the Hololive brand.   Earlier in the song, she mentions that she "wretches endlessly about their excuses" and complaints, well... I imagine for anybody who joins a company like Hololive which places higher demands and standards on your work, seeing someone go "Easy for you to say, Little Miss Company Hire" would make them wretch because it's so wrong and ironic. Hololive does have perks, but yet it comes with _responsibilities_ and more work. Hololive gives better rewards, but yet requires more work. It doesn't make your life easier.   I've not seen anybody in comments raising this point about that part of the lyrics, so I thought I'd offer that here. I don't know if that's what her intended meaning behind that line was or not, but that's simply how I interpreted it.

Everything about this song is pretty fire. Lyrically it is straight forward and extremely relatable. The pace is synonym to the effort and dedication required to succeed in competition. Overall everything about this song makes me go "Yeah, this is a pretty good song."  But then there is that one line "Welcome to the mountaintop" and its delivery in particular. I just can't get over how good that one line is delivered.  Even at the top the fight goes on. There is no sense of having achieved a set destination. So you reached the top? So what, think you're done now? There is only greed for more challenge. This fight is eternal. It's not about the mountaintop, it's all about the fight.  Calli could have delivered the line more deadpan like some of the other lines. Like, 'here we are'. But she doesn't. There is greed, passion and it is even issuing a challenge in the way she delivered that particular line. And it is exactly that which makes that line soooo fucking good.  Without that line, this song would have been a great song, but 'just' a great song. With that line this song is made eternal.

REPORT IN THE FINE ARTS SECTION OF THE NEWSPAPER Regrettably, all too often, access to the public is facilitated for so-called "artists," who, being reckless agitators and imitators in the service of radical Left machinations, then have to conceal their dilettantism and their lack of ability under the shoddy pretext of an allegedly "modern trend." This time, however, we were dealing with a master who must be taken seriously and who was outstanding in his ability to interpret the ups and downs of moods in the various stages of life, an interpretation as joyful and life-affirming, friendly and outgoing, high-spirited and expressive, as it was driven by a towering sense of mission, of moving spiritual engagement, profound earnestness, purest serenity, and unparalleled inner composure. The drummer had walked through the narrow streets to gather the people. The people stood in a circle in the village square. To begin, the artist gave a small sample of his ability. He had two assistants take position and gave them a thick iron rod, whose ends they held at chest height. Then the artist went back about five steps and dashed with such suddenness and unbelievable ferocity toward the rod - no one would have thought it remotely possible - the rod was bent completely out of shape. The people were enthusiastic and applauded vigorously. The technical perfection and elegance of the artist received general admiration and lively comment. The two able assistants, without whose trustworthy steadfastness the first item on the program could not have succeeded, also deserve favorable mention. The two upright lads proved their mettle; they really have to be strong, tor the artist undoubtedly would have flung them and the rod through the audience and against the nearest house.  For the next item on the program the artist took a chain, wrapped it around his chest, and, urged on by the crescendo of the drum roll, expanded the latter in such a powerful way that - no one would have thought it possible - a link of the chain burst, the chain let go of his chest and fell rattling to the ground. The audience responded with hearty applause. Special admiration, as well as lively discussion and comment, were elicited by the sparkling vitality of the artist; it was the general consensus that he was a master in his field. For the enxt item on his program the artist took a large thick coil, fastened it to the ground, put the upper end of the coil between his teeth, and pulled on it with his teeth so tenaciously and vigorously that - no one would have thought it possible - the coil was pulled apart. The audience was thrilled, there was vigorous clapping and enthusiastic applause. General admiration, discussion, and comment were also elicited by the artist's great empathy, as well as the versatility of the repertoire he has in stock. One can do naught but proclaim: Well done, indeed! Our master, who, throughout the entire truly comprehensive program, was really in excellent form, proved completely capable of giving his wide-ranging yet solid offerings a cloak of mysticism and of manifesting transfiguration and purification so that it was obvious to all that here was a man who, because of his acquired maturity, has achieved his expertise fair and square, by hard work and unflagging industry. The high point and conclusion of the program consisted of the so-called "tightrope walk." The two able assistants, even before the start of the performance, had stretched a rope from the top of a tree across the village square, to the top of a tree standing opposite, some eight meters (!) above the ground. The artist climbed up the tree, attained the height of the rope, positioned himself properly on the rope and began, slowly and carefully putting one foot in front of the other, to cross the village square on the rope in the air (!). The tree limb on whose tip the rope was fastened was so overloaded by the weight of the artist that it broke, and the rope, with him, plummeted to the ground. The artist had at that moment been in the air above the well and our master fell from the heavens in such a way that - no one would have that it remotely possible - his back landed precisely on the crossbar of the well winch, his spinal column thus breaking exactly in the middle (!) so that his body, snapped in two, dangled over the well. The people were completely carried away, responded with enthusiastic applause, and burst into frenetic demonstrations of approval. General admiration, discussion, and comment were also elicited by the artist's quiet modesty and restrained manner. At last, once again, here was someone, who, by virtue of his noble character, his soul-sitting worldly wisdom, his exquisite and subtle humor, has no need to embrace those leftist, negativistic, modernistic tendencies which aid certain subversive elements, who, in the fateful and false guise of "art," would like nothing better than to undermine the natural order, the healthy discipline, and the simple sensitivity of our people, but they will not succeed, for we have seen once again that there were still people with  b a c k b o n e  and character, who speak to the public from the depth of their souls, whose hearts are in the right place, who know their oats, and who know what's what. Pretty bold song, but quite on point: the people who want success but not do all the painful work towards it will only feel frustration and jealousy - they only see "luck" when someone make it big, and conveniently forget about the 10,000 times that same person gave everything they could to get a single chance.  Not everyone win the lottery, but those who earn their ticket every day months after months have a much bigger chance at winning something in the long run. As far as I know Calli didn't start swinging yesterday, she went back to the salt mines for years, her current success is her long awaited harvest.  If someone truly wants to go into that business, they better starting planting seeds now and expect to starve in the first 2 years at the very least, it's a ruthless job and a risky choice that demands a huge sacrifice. If someone's not ready to do it out of passion for years, only accepting to endure it because of expected quick profits and celebrity, it's not going to work.  That's the rule for anything that involves an audience, bet it cinema, singing, music, photography, painting or even sport - most people in these sectors have another job to pay the bills and it takes years of hard work to finally get a seat at the table.   Aspiring candidates in all these sectors burn so much money on manufacturing what they think would be the best portfolio to get hired up and launched into success, missing the fact that five thousands bucks won't buy you the experience and confidence in your work that five years doing that job yourself will.
hard work doesn't guarantee success, but success requires hard work, and you can't complain about a lack of success if you aren't putting in the work in the first place.

Trending at #30, Calli slaying Youtube with her fire spitting.
In any creative field, budget and resources only can take you so far. Having the most advanced model, god-tier art, an overlay that works like magic, the NASA supercomputer, and an unlimited budget certainly helps. But if the voice behind all that isn't good, all you've made is a glorified tech-demo. In order to really make it in the creative industry, you have to do what the name implies: be creative. Think outside the box and work around your limitations while playing to your strengths. Avatar sucks ass and your art looks like trash? Get good at games or singing. Is your PC a potato and your internet is garbage? Prerecord your streams and make highlight compilations. Need to work a side-job to pay the bills? Make what few streams you have memorable and make the time. If it cuts into your sleep-schedule or social life, than so be it. If this is your passion, than you should be prepared to make sacrifices for it. If you have the means to record and upload what you make, than you already have everything you need.  Suisei came from the fucing dirt when vtuber premieres got you nothing, and ended up becoming a household name. Outside of vtubers, the biggest indie games of the past few years have been a point-and-click game running on an engine worse than unity and an rpg-maker game with garbage pixel art. There is no excuse for you to not make something. If you make nothing, all you are is a pretender who takes attention away from people who actually try.  At the end of the day, all creative products are selling you an idea, and the tools used to make it is just the means by which that idea is conveyed. If your idea is bad, it won't get far. If your idea is good, it will be spread. If you have no idea, you will get nowhere. Until you put out your idea, you have nothing, will get nothing and deserve nothing.  So you wanna make it as a v-tuber? Become one first.

zero two calli
Hey, Mori, not sure you'll ever see this, but I need to tell you something. I've been wanting to create since I was barely a teenager. Before, even. I always struggled with motivation, and a big part of it was a belief that was drilled into me that creating on youtube wasn't a real job, or that I'd never be able to make a successful comic, and that all the people out there like you were exceptions, not the rule. I went to engineering school for 2 and a half years, convincing myself I was happy with something I didn't enjoy, until I had a mental breakdown and had to switch majors. I haven't been the same since then. I've had intense anxiety and my depression has gotten worse. It sometimes feels like all I can do to put in 10 hours a week at the grocery store and take 6 credits of classes. And that took me 2 years of recovery to build up to. I've been picking away at my passions during that time, but it's been slow.  I don't know what it is, but there's something about you and your lyrics that speaks to me. I feel like we've felt some of the same things, and it means a lot to me seeing you succeed. And the lyrics of this video really reached me, I want you to know. I don't know how long it'll be till I have it in me to 'swing till the sunrise' so to speak, but I'm getting better every day. And I think this song is going to help.  Just wanted you to know that you're making a difference in my life.

"This b!tch has no talent! She was just hired by a big company!" "She got lucky that she got hired" "Easy life, they handled her a big name from start!" "She just sit there for X hours and make $XXXX !"  Heads are rolling, but it didn't have to be like that. She's not attacking, she just wanted to do her thing, but "past tense on reservations now I stand in defense", because once on the mountain top, it doesn't matter if you're looking for fights, just wait a little and they'll come.   If you're going to throw a rock, be prepared to receive one back, but most importantly, why did you feel the need to go out of your way to attack someone in the first place? Don't be pretentious, look at yourself. Especially if you want to be a critic of the industry, the system, society, whatever, if you do that while upholding hypocrisy, you're just doing worse for your onw cause. It's easy to point and judge, but more often than not, we're just pointing at our own demons. Internet and anonymity makes it easy for anyone to say anything and feel validated, but when talking about others, their lives, their experiences, we hardly know any sh!t about whoever we're talking about. We gotta learn to be humble, remind ourselves constantly to stay humble. Going a bit further on the tangent, this reminded me of the quote "every saint has a past and every sinner has a future" (Oscar WIlde, A Woman of no Importance)... It's easy to look at someone's success and forget about their path to reach it, their origin. And it's easy to, being a "sinner" on our own personal hells, fall prey to our "sins" and delve in discontent and envy, forgetting this doesn' t have to be our final stage and we still have a future. There's a way out, so pursue it. But yeah, I'm already digressing a lot, lol.   Why am I even writing this? No idea, actually, I'm mostly self reflecting about the lyrics of this amazing song. It's unfortunate and ironic that the people who most needed to get this reality check from Calli will probably just take it as "uh-oh, she's hating on me" or if they understand their pride will blind them of their own condition. But even for me that have respected and admired her work from the start this is a valuable message, and I thank her for creating this great song. It's meanings are valid for way more situations, it's a good life lesson. You're really inspiring, Calli!!!  Thanks, Dad, keep on going on this journey, we'll be here to support you on this path, as you're here to help us when we need it too!

I really think that everyone can appreciate Calli's tough love message, especially  It's not enough to simply say "I want this really badly, so I deserve to get it". That is NOT enough. You need to WORK for it.   I've always wanted to work with animals ever since I was a child. It's always been my passion, and I'm very fortunate to say that several years back I was able to achieve that dream. But it sure as sugar didn't happen overnight. Whether it was watching every documentary and reading every book I could get my hands on,  building up as much first hand experience as possible, or working and learning all I could during college, volunteering, and even STILL while working on the job, I've worked to try and hammer and forge myself into who I am today. My managers often say "You never stop being a student", and I completely agree.  And when you work both with animals AND the general public like my coworkers and I (I work in a science museum, and many of my fellow staff members have also worked in zoos and other similar establishments), you NEED to be effective on dealing with both. Especially children. If you don't know something, they WILL call you out on it!  Which is in itself is an important "teachable moment" in never being afraid to admit you don't know something and find an appropriate solution.   Which is precisely why I get really frustrated with the mindset some people have towards not putting in the work. Yes, passion and faith are important, and can be great for helping to fuel whatever drive you have, or goal you aspire to.  But your actions have to speak louder than words. If you're nothing but talk and no work ethic, you won't get anywhere. That's like a sword smith  complaining about not being able to forge a sword, when all he did was talk himself up and not gather metal, stoke his forge, hammer the metal into shape, etc.   I'm hoping plenty of deadbeats come to the realization that Calli is talking about.  She truly does want the best for us, and this is just a more brutally honest method of giving that push in the right direction.

Throwing shade and swinging that heavy scythe while spitting fire left and right, Calli's new song's meant to burn the living, the dead and everyone along. She ended all pretenders, offenders and unpassionate vtuber descendants by simply asking "what's the use of a body for a head that does not act to get ahead?"  And thus, I mirror her question: is there even a need to mention all the attention that laughable pretension is giving to the aforementioned congregation, when a simple action (and not a retraction) with the intent of gaining enough traction to elicit a positive reaction is sure to bring us all satisfaction?  If her words go unheeded, it's not because they're unneded but probably superceded by both fear and regret, lest we forget we all started in the red and the climb out of the net of the inaction mindset required our very own initial step (which was more like a bet), and through slips and falls and tears and joys we learned about courage, about practice, about perfection and such antics.  So yeah: this song is about tough love, but love nonetheless. 'Cuz at the end of the day, you're responsible for your success.     Gotta admit, I had fun writing this

Becoming a vtuber under a company already well known for their vtuber talent is obviously fucking great. But it also got drawbacks, mostly in the form of "requirement".  Lots of people dream to be one. Anyone with an internet can just start tweet as one. Anyone with a voice can just talk like one. Anyone with a couple of coin can afford a cheap avatar and truly become one. But lots of these people stop at step two. Even more stop at step one. And they had the gal to say any of the hologirls and holostars have it easy? They manage to fight off the hundred or maybe even thousand other candidate. A lot of them start off by themself, as just another candle in a sea of glowing star. The first of these girls, while dont have nearly as much rivals, they have it even harder. They have no base. They can do nothing but just hope either god, luck or algorithm favor them. They persevere through lots of trials, in order to build the base their junior can use. They all have gone through and fight off a lot more than someone that cant even take that third step.

A really different thematic song compared to your original ones... like how Cursed Night was a more toned down departure from your debut songs, this song is a more EDM/eastern motivated. The genre diversity is really interesting!   In regard to the aspects of the song itself, I noticed that this song incorporates less bilingual lyrics, has very interesting instrumentals/sounds, and had a very interesting flow (?). You didn't use your "chorus"/"hook" that much even though it was really catchy and chose to focus on the rap bits of your song (and chose to use less bilingual lyrics)--which really emphasizes what kind of song this one is.   Listening to it for the first time, I didn't know what to expect, so I was a bit thrown off. Now having listened to it a few times and now that I know what to expect, this song has really grown on me! Overall, I really like it! I hope it didn't come off like I disliked it nor that I was critiquing it, because I hardly know a thing about music! I just wanted to comment on a few things I noticed and appreciated!   Also, I know you mentioned you were unsure about releasing a song like Cursed Night again, but I hope you now realize that us Dead Beats will support you no matter what you put out, as long as you're proud of it!
